               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The electrochemical reaction products during the electrode cycling process over a wide temperature range from −40 to 60 °C are further identified using TEM (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25–S27</a>, Supporting Information). HRTEM and SAED images reveal that when the electrode is first charged to 3&nbsp;V, besides Mo nanocrystals, the FeS<sub>2</sub> nanocrystals (≈3&nbsp;nm) appear, confirming that the oxidation product of Fe<sup>0</sup> is FeS<sub>2</sub>. The irreversibility of Mo would result in the existence of elemental S after full desodiation of Na<sub>2</sub>S due to the higher atomic content of Mo than Fe (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). Obviously, the crystal lattice and diffraction ring of S do not appear (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25b, S26b</a>, and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27b</a>, Supporting Information), indicating the residual S is amorphous. This result indicates the electrode after full desodiation contains Mo nanocrystals, FeS<sub>2</sub> nanocrystals, and amorphous S. After 100 cycles, when the electrode is discharged to 0.01&nbsp;V, the reaction products are Mo nanocrystals, Fe nanocrystals, and Na<sub>2</sub>S nanocrystals (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25c,d, S26c,d</a>, and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27c,d</a>, Supporting Information), consistent with the products after the first discharge. Similarly, when the electrode is charged to 3&nbsp;V after 100 cycles, the reaction products are Mo nanocrystals, FeS<sub>2</sub> nanocrystals, and amorphous S (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25e,f, S26e,f</a>, and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27e,f</a>, Supporting Information), identical to those after the first charge. Consequently, Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C is that the doped Fe atoms and MoS<sub>2</sub> can be converted into Fe, Mo, and Na<sub>2</sub>S nanocrystals during first sodiation process, and the Fe can be oxidated into FeS<sub>2</sub> but Mo does not, leading to residues of amorphous S during desodiation process. In the subsequent sodiation process, the FeS<sub>2</sub> and S can be converted into Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S, which can continue to form FeS<sub>2</sub> and S in the desodiation process. It is noteworthy that although the Mo° formed after the initial discharge does not directly participate in subsequent electrochemical reactions, the metallic Mo<sup>0</sup> uniformly dispersed within the electrode material significantly enhances the electron transfer capability of the electrode. This improvement facilitates the achievement of high rate capacity under large current densities. Additionally, Mo<sup>0</sup> particles with an approximate size of 2&nbsp;nm possess an extremely large specific surface area. The numerous Mo<sup>0</sup> particles provide the electrode material with a substantial number of interfaces, which can serve as additional Na<sup>+</sup> storage sites, thereby increasing the specific capacity of the electrode material.</p>
            
            <p>Taking into account that 1) the formed ≈2&nbsp;nm Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals possess superparamagnetic properties,<sup>16</sup> and 2) magnetic properties are highly sensitive to electronic transfer, phase composition, and structural changes of transition metals and their compounds,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0042_R_d35498333e1795" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Energy Environ. Sci.">42</a>, <a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0043_R_d35498333e1795" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Adv. Mater.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> we conduct further investigations on the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism of the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode using in situ magnetometry at 25&nbsp;°C. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0003">3f</a> depicts the variation in magnetization of the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode with changes in electrode potential and cycling time during the initial three cycles. During the initial discharge process, the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode exhibits an almost negligible magnetization change from open circuit voltage to ≈1.0&nbsp;V, which falls into the voltage range of the occurrence of intercalation reaction. The result demonstrates that the intercalation reaction does not cause the apparent change of electrode magnetization. When discharge from 1 to 0.45&nbsp;V, the magnetization shows a sharp increase and reaches a maximum at ≈0.45&nbsp;V. The voltage range corresponds to the occurrence of the conversion reaction, and thus the rapid increase of the electrode magnetization is attributed to the generation of superparamagnetic Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals. Remarkably, the magnetization experiences a decrease in the low-voltage range of 0.45-0.01&nbsp;V during the ongoing discharge and a subsequent increase in the voltage range of 0.01–1.08&nbsp;V during the charging process. This can be explained as follows: since the d-orbit electrons of Fe are not full, once the superparamagnetic Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals are formed during the conversion process, numerous spin-polarized electrons are injected into their d orbits under the magnetic field. Therefore, Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals act as an electron-accepting phase, while Na<sub>2</sub>S serves as the acceptor phase for Na<sup>+</sup>. This results in the separation of charges at the interfaces between Fe<sup>0</sup> and Na<sub>2</sub>S, leading to the formation of a space charge zone. This phenomenon is referred to as the “work-sharing” mechanism,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0044_R_d35498333e1828" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Nat. Energy">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which can provide extra capacity and accelerate charge transfer. Additionally, the extra spin-polarized electrons are mainly stored in spin-down d bands of Fe<sup>0</sup>, thus decreasing the magnetization.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0016_R_d35498333e1835" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Nat. Mater.">16</a>, <a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0021_R_d35498333e1835" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The charging process can be regarded as a reverse progression, where magnetization increases with the escape of spin-polarized electrons from the d orbits of Fe<sup>0</sup> within the voltage range of 0.01–1.08&nbsp;V. The observed magnetic variations above demonstrate the presence of the spin-polarized surface capacitance originating from superparamagnetic Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals in the low potential range of 0.01–1&nbsp;V. Subsequently, a significant decrease in magnetization is observed when charging from 1.08 to 2.13&nbsp;V due to gradual oxidation of Fe into FeS<sub>2</sub>. In contrast to the first cycle, in subsequent cycles, the initial voltage of the conversion reaction increases from 1.01 to 1.56&nbsp;V and its corresponding cut-off voltage decreases from 0.45 to 0.33&nbsp;V, and the cut-off voltage of the oxidation reaction increases from 2.13 to 2.26&nbsp;V. This shift is attributed to that the formed FeS<sub>2</sub> in the first cycle has higher initial conversion voltage and cut-off oxidation voltage than MoS<sub>2</sub>. In the 2nd and 3rd cycles, the magnetization variation trend remains consistent, and the initial and cut-off potentials of both the conversion and oxidation reactions remain constant. This consistency indicates the reversibility and stability of the magnetic response and sodium-ion storage mechanism during electrochemical reaction processes.</p>
            
            <p>To demonstrate the formation of superparamagnetic Fe nanocrystals during conversion reaction at −40 and 60&nbsp;°C, we perform ex situ TEM observations on the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrodes. Clearly, from HRTEM images and SAED patterns, Fe nanocrystals (≈2&nbsp;nm) are formed after discharging to 0.01&nbsp;V at −40&nbsp;°C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0003">3g,h</a>) and 60&nbsp;°C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0003">3j,k</a>) and are evenly distributed in the electrodes (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a> for −40&nbsp;°C and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29</a>, Supporting Information for 60&nbsp;°C), which shows similar results with that at 25&nbsp;°C and indicates superparamagnetic Fe conversion over a wide temperature range. In our previous reports, spin-polarized surface capacitance has been confirmed, which can occur on the surface of superparamagnetic 3d transition metal nanocrystals at room temperature.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0016_R_d35498333e1869" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Nat. Mater.">16</a>, <a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0017_R_d35498333e1869" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Matter">17</a>, <a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0021_R_d35498333e1869" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the evolution of the spin-polarized surface capacitance at high and low battery operating temperatures remains unknown. To explore this evolution, in situ magnetometry is conducted on the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrodes operating at −40 and 60 °C. Obviously, the voltage-dependent magnetic response, akin to which is observed at 25 °C, is also present in electrode operating at −40 °C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0003">3i</a>) and 60 °C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0003">3l</a>). Therefore, it can be asserted that the spin-polarized surface capacitance effect in electrodes can operate effectively from −40 to 60 °C. Unlike the magnetic response observed at 25&nbsp;°C, the electrode, when operating at −40&nbsp;°C, experiences an increase in the initial voltage of the conversion reaction from 1.01 to 1.49&nbsp;V. Concurrently, the corresponding cut-off voltage decreases from 0.45 to 0.31&nbsp;V, while the cut-off voltage of the oxidation reaction rises from 2.13 to 3&nbsp;V. This can be attributed to an increase in electrode polarization (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0002">2e</a>) and a decrease in reaction kinetics (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0002">2j</a>) at −40&nbsp;°C. Operating at a high temperature of 60&nbsp;°C, the reaction voltages during the 1st cycle closely resemble those at 25&nbsp;°C. Specifically, the conversion reaction voltage is slightly elevated, and the initial oxidation reaction voltage is marginally lower. This subtle variation is attributed to a slight reduction in electrode polarization at 60&nbsp;°C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0002">2e</a>) and an enhancement in reaction kinetics at this temperature (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0002">2j</a>). Obviously, from the cut-off voltage of the conversion reaction to 0.01&nbsp;V, and then to the starting voltage of the oxidation reaction, the amplitude of the change in electrode magnetization decreases with the reduction of temperature (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0003">3f,i,l</a>). This is because the reduction of temperature leads to a decrease in charge diffusion kinetics, which results in a decrease in the injection number of spin-polarized electrons into Fe, thus causing a decrease in the amplitude of changes in electrode magnetization. From the GITT curves (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0002">2i,j</a>) above, during the discharge process, the higher <i>D<sub>Na+</sub></i> values center about between 0.5 and 0.01&nbsp;V, and during the charging process, the higher values are about between 0.01–1&nbsp;V, which correspond to the voltage range of the formation and disappearance of spin-polarized surface capacitance. This result further indicates that spin-polarized surface capacitance is conducive to the rapid transport of ions over a wide temperature range of −40-60&nbsp;°C. Note that we also utilize in situ magnetometry to monitor the changes in magnetization of the MoS<sub>2</sub>/C electrodes during cycling at −40&nbsp;°C (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30</a>, Supporting Information), 25&nbsp;°C (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S31</a>, Supporting Information), and 60&nbsp;°C (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S32</a>, Supporting Information), and find that its magnetization remains close to zero and almost constant throughout the cycling at various temperatures. This further implies that the variations in magnetization during cycling for the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrodes are attributed to superparamagnetic Fe conversion. In other words, 4d transition metal Mo cannot cause change of electrode magnetization to induce spin-polarized surface capacitance but 3d transition metal Fe can. The above results confirm that the conversion-type sodium storage mechanism of the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode operates effectively over the temperature range of −40 to 60 °C, and the doped Fe atoms in MoS<sub>2</sub> lattices can be converted into superparamagnetic Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals (≈2&nbsp;nm) to induce strong spin-polarized surface capacitance, which can store extra ions and boost charge transport, thus supplying extra capacity and improving fast-charging performance.</p>
            
            <p>The sodium storage of electrode material arises from intercalation and conversion reaction of FeMoS<sub>2</sub> and the carbon materials. The sodium ion storage of interfaces mainly arises from space charge storage at the interfaces of Fe/Na<sub>2</sub>S and the intercalation reaction between FeMoS<sub>2</sub> and monolayer carbon and between conversion products and carbon matrix. To identify the contribution of the interface and the electrode material to the sodium storage capacity, we also conducted performance tests on pure carbon materials synthesized from pyrolysis of CH<sub>3</sub>C(O)N(CH<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub> under the same conditions with FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C. We take the second cycle as an example to rule out the impact of large irreversible capacity during the sodiation process in the first cycle. The second-cycle charge and discharge curves of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II and carbon materials are shown in Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S33</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S34</a> (Supporting Information), respectively. The corresponding capacity contributions at different key-point voltages are summarized in Tables <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15–S17</a> (Supporting Information). The interfacial sodium storage between FeMoS<sub>2</sub> and carbon and between conversion products of FeMoS<sub>2</sub> and carbon exists throughout the entire voltage range, which coexists with intercalation and conversion process of the electrode materials, thus resulting in its inability to be calculated separately. To simplify the discussion, we only consider that interface sodium storage is caused by space charge storage at the interfaces of Fe/Na<sub>2</sub>S. The capacity contribution of space charge storage at the interfaces of Fe/Na<sub>2</sub>S at −40&nbsp;°C (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a>, Supporting Information), 25&nbsp;°C (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a>, Supporting Information), and 60&nbsp;°C (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information) can be calculated as 140.8, 233.5, and 210.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, and the corresponding capacity contribution of electrode materials is 429.2, 486.5, and 517 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. It can be seen that the interface sodium storage plays an important role in the total capacity.</p>
            
            <p>It is essential to note that the presence of the monolayer carbon in Fe-MoS<sub>2</sub>-NOC is crucial for the formation of these ultra-small Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals. As observed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S35</a> (Supporting Information), for pure MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode after discharging to 0.01&nbsp;V, the size of the formed Mo<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals is ≈10&nbsp;nm. When introducing the monolayer MoS<sub>2</sub> and monolayer C overlapping structure, the formed Mo<sup>0</sup> and/or Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals after discharging to 0.01&nbsp;V have a size of ≈2&nbsp;nm for MoS<sub>2</sub>/C (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S36</a>), FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-I (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S37</a>, Supporting Information), FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0003">3d</a>), and FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-III (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S38a</a>, Supporting Information). Clearly, for FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-III, besides 2&nbsp;nm nanocrystals, the Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals with the size of ≈7&nbsp;nm (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S38b</a>, Supporting Information) also appear due to the presence of Fe<sub>1-x</sub>S phase in FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-III, in addition to Fe-MoS<sub>2</sub>-NOC. Within MoS<sub>2</sub>-NOC or Fe-MoS<sub>2</sub>-NOC, the monolayer carbon serves a confining role by preventing adjacent Mo and/or Fe atoms in the MoS<sub>2</sub> layers from interacting, thereby suppressing the growth of Mo<sup>0</sup> and/or Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals during the conversion reaction. In contrast, in pure MoS<sub>2</sub> or Fe<sub>1-x</sub>S phase, the absence of monolayer carbon's confining effect allows Mo or Fe atoms to freely grow into larger-sized Mo<sup>0</sup> or Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals. Emphatically the size of 3d transition metal nanocrystals plays a crucial role in inducing the spin-polarized surface capacitance effect, which weakens as the size of the 3d transition metal nanocrystals increases and cannot be induced when their size exceeds 10&nbsp;nm.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0016_R_d35498333e2055" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Nat. Mater.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Consequently, the successful construction of Fe-MoS<sub>2</sub>-NOC is conducive to the formation of smaller Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals (≈2&nbsp;nm), facilitating the induction of a stronger spin-polarized surface capacitance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0016_R_d35498333e2065" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Nat. Mater.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Furthermore, considering the high catalytic activity of Fe and Mo nanoparticles, we analyze the SEI films of MoS<sub>2</sub>, MoS<sub>2</sub>/C, and FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrodes after 20 cycles using depth-profiling XPS (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S39–S41</a>, Supporting Information). Na 1s and F 1s spectra are obtained at different Ar<sup>+</sup> sputtering times. The two overlapping peaks (Na-O and Na-F) in Na 1s spectra reveal the presence of inorganic Na compounds in the SEI films. The SEI film of the MoS<sub>2</sub>/C electrode exhibits an obviously increased content of F─P bonds compared to the MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode. This is likely due to the higher catalytic activity of the smaller Mo nanoparticles (≈2&nbsp;nm) in the MoS<sub>2</sub>/C electrode, compared to the ≈10&nbsp;nm Mo nanoparticles in the MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode. In the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode, although both Fe and Mo particles are ≈2&nbsp;nm in size, the introduction of Fe nanoparticles significantly suppresses the F─P bond content in the SEI film, resulting in the lowest F─P bond content compared to MoS<sub>2</sub>/C and MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode. This indicates that Fe nanoparticles help inhibit the formation of F─P bonds in the SEI film, thereby increasing the content of F─Na bonds. According to previous reports,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0045_R_d35498333e2097" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Adv. Mater.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> NaF in the SEI has several advantages, including electronic insulation to limit subsequent parasitic reactions and a high Young's modulus, which contributes to the stability of the SEI film. This is confirmed by the higher coulombic efficiency exhibited by the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode during cycling (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S42</a>, Supporting Information). It is noteworthy that Ar<sup>+</sup> sputtering tests indicate the SEI layer thickness on the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode exceeds 15&nbsp;nm after 20 cycles. Compared to previous reports, this thickness falls within a reasonable range.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0046_R_d35498333e2112" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - ACS Energy Lett.">46</a>-<a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0048_R_d35498333e2112" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - ACS Cent. Sci.">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Although a relatively thick SEI layer might intuitively seem to hinder Na<sup>+</sup> transport, it is also important to consider the SEI layer composition. The SEI layer on the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode contains substantial amounts of Na-O and Na-F species, which can create pathways that allow more efficient Na<sup>+</sup> migration, thereby facilitating Na<sup>+</sup> transport through the SEI layer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0049_R_d35498333e2126" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Energy Environ. Sci.">49</a>-<a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0052_R_d35498333e2126" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S43</a> (Supporting Information), after 100 cycles at 60 °C, the peak shapes of the C 1s, F 1s, and Na 1s spectra of the SEI film on the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode nearly overlap with those from the first cycle. This demonstrates that the composition and content of the SEI film remain largely unchanged during prolonged cycling, confirming the structure stability of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II at high operating temperature. Furthermore, within the operating temperature range of −40 to 60 °C, after 100 cycles at 0.1 C (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25c,d, S26c,d</a>, and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27c,d</a>, Supporting Information) and 1000 cycles at 2 C (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S44</a>, Supporting Information), the ultra-small Fe/Mo nanocrystals remained stably dispersed in the carbon matrix, maintaining a morphology similar to that observed after the first discharge to 0.01&nbsp;V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0003">3d,g,j</a>). This demonstrates the excellent dispersibility and stability of the Fe nanoparticles in the electrode during long-term cycling. According to above results, it is believed that metallic Fe<sup>0</sup> nanocrystals, originating from the conversion of Fe atoms doped into the MoS<sub>2</sub> lattice during the conversion reaction, are favor to the stability of the SEI film and continue to be actively involved in the electrochemically driven sodiation process in the form of spin-polarized surface capacitance.</p>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">To fully understand the kinetic properties of spin-polarized surface capacitance caused by superparamagnetic Fe conversion, we carry out the CV tests with voltages from 0.01 to 1&nbsp;V and scanning rates from 0.1 to 20&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. The selection of a cut-off voltage of 1&nbsp;V is based on the starting voltages of the oxidation reaction, which are 1.49, 1.08, and 1.06&nbsp;V at −40, 25, and 60&nbsp;°C, respectively. This result indicates that no oxidation of superparamagnetic Fe occurs when charged to 1&nbsp;V, which means no oxidation-reduction reaction in the voltage range of 0.01–1&nbsp;V. This provides convenience for exploring spin-polarized surface capacitance caused by superparamagnetic Fe conversion. In the voltage range of 0.01–1&nbsp;V, besides the space charge storage at the interfaces of Fe/Na<sub>2</sub>S, other sodium storage behaviors mainly include the interface sodium storage between FeMoS<sub>2</sub> and carbon and between conversion products and carbon, sodium adsorption on the defective surface of N,O co-doped carbon, and insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> in the stacked carbon layers. Both interface and defective adsorption sodium storage belong to the capacitive contribution. Insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> in the stacked short-range carbon layers belongs to diffusion process, but its capacity contribution proportion is significantly weak, which may be due to the low synthesis temperature. Based on the above discussions, the ≈100% capacitive contribution can be achieved from the voltage range of 0.01–1&nbsp;V. Furthermore, as shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S34</a> and Tables <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15-S17</a> (Supporting Information), at operating temperatures of −40, 25, and 60 °C, the specific capacity of the carbon component in FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II in the low voltage range of 0.01–1&nbsp;V is significantly lower than that of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II in the same voltage range. Therefore, the contribution of the carbon component to the electrode capacity in the 0.01–1&nbsp;V voltage range can be considered negligible. Clearly, the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrodes operated at −40 °C (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0004">4a</a>), 25 °C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0004">4c</a>), and 60 °C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0004">4e</a>) show rectangular CV curves representing capacitive behavior, which can be determined based on the Equation&nbsp;(<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#adfm202404263-disp-0002" title="Link to equation">2</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0053_R_d35498333e2198" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Small">53</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202404263-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                     <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/1a792e3b-d163-4cfb-942d-5aa767a1746f/adfm202404263-math-0002.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202404263:adfm202404263-math-0002" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202404263-math-0002.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <mrow>
                              <mi>log</mi>
                              <mi>i</mi>
                              <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                              <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                              <mi>b</mi>
                              <mi>log</mi>
                              <mi>v</mi>
                              <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                              <mi>log</mi>
                              <mi>a</mi>
                           </mrow>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}\log i = \ b\log v + \log a\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>where <i>i</i> is current, <i>v</i> is scan rate, <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> are empirical constants. The <i>b</i>-values of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode are approximately equal to 1 (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S45a,c,e</a>, Supporting Information), demonstrating that the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode has an absolute capacitive response over a wide range of operating temperatures between 0.01 and 1&nbsp;V. As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S45b,d,f</a>, and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a> (Supporting Information), the proportion of capacitive contribution of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode is ≈100% from 0.1 to 20.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> when operated at −40–60 °C. The results confirm that the spin-polarized surface capacitance effect totally dominates Na-ion storage in the low potential range of 0.01–1.0&nbsp;V, which is further revealed by in situ magnetometry in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0004">4b</a> for −40 °C, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0004">4d</a> for 25 °C, and Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0004">4f</a> for 60 °C. The magnetization of the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode increases during charging from 0.01 to 1&nbsp;V, and subsequently decreases during discharging from 1 to 0.01&nbsp;V at −40-60 °C. This finding highlights good reversibility of the capacitive behaviors involving superparamagnetic Fe<sup>0</sup>.</div>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202404263-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/28066885-8997-4ee1-b7d3-1758a48ab028/adfm202404263-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/28066885-8997-4ee1-b7d3-1758a48ab028/adfm202404263-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/68567c9e-d259-4c42-ae73-c2b99ffb3074/adfm202404263-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/28066885-8997-4ee1-b7d3-1758a48ab028/adfm202404263-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202404263-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202404263" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The electrochemical kinetic analysis of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrodes at −40, 25, and 60 °C from 0.01 to 1.0 V: CV curves at a) −40, c) 25, and e) 60 °C. In situ magnetometry at operating temperatures of b) −40, d) 25, and f) 60 °C from 0.01 to 1.0&nbsp;V.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202404263-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202404263-sec-0060-title">2.4 Electrochemical Performances of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II in Full Cells</h3>
            
            <p>As a practical demonstration, we evaluate the electrochemical performances of full coin cells utilizing FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II as anode and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as cathode over a wide operating temperature range, which obtain impressive first discharge capacities of 113.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 60 °C, 108.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 25 °C, and 66.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at −40 °C (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0005">5a</a>). Furthermore, after 100 cycles at 0.1 C, there is no noticeable capacity decay (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0005">5b</a>), underscoring the excellent cyclic stability of the full coin cells across the broad operation temperature range. In Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0005">5c</a>, we present the rate performance, with the full coin cell at 60 °C slightly outperforming its rate capacity compared to the 25 °C case, consistent with the results in the half cells. Even under extremely challenging low-temperature conditions (−40 °C), the full coin cell maintains robust rate performance, offering 47.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 1 C (equivalent to 50.3% of the capacity at 25 °C) and 30.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 3 C (equivalent to 38.3% of the capacity at 25 °C). Additionally, the full coin cells exhibit gravimetric energy densities of 108.7&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at −40 °C, 185.4&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 25 °C, and 200.6&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 60 °C. Charging at 3 C for 7.8&nbsp;min at −40 °C results in an energy density of 42.6&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0005">5d</a>). At an elevated operating temperature of 25 °C, charging for 14.1&nbsp;min at 3 C yields an energy density of 130.9&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0005">5e</a>), which is 70.6% of that at 0.1 C. Remarkably, when operating at 60 °C, with the same current density and charging time as at 25 °C, the energy density can reach as high as 139.3&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0005">5f</a>), highlighting the remarkable fast-charging capability of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II across a wide operation temperature range. In addition, we conduct long-term cycling tests to evaluate the battery's lifespan. After 1000 cycles at 1 C, the capacity retentions at −40, 25, and 60 °C are 75.5%, 72.2%, and 63.7%, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0005">5g</a>). Evidently, capacity retention increases as the operating temperature decreases, possibly due to slower electrolyte degradation at lower temperatures.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202404263-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202404263-bib-0025_R_d35498333e2361" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Chem. Commun.">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This result confirms the excellent long-term cycling durability of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II as a full-coin-cell anode within a wide operation temperature range. Compared to recently reported full coin cells when MoS<sub>2</sub>-based materials as anodes, our FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II║Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> full cell exhibits a significant advantage in capacity and cycling stability at room temperature (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a>, Supporting Information). Furthermore, this full coin cell successfully powers an array of light-emitting diodes (LEDs, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0005">5h</a>). Additionally, the full coin cell with higher cathode active material loading of 10.5&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S46</a>, Supporting Information) and the 1 Ah capacity FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II║Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> pouch full cell (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S47</a>, Supporting Information) also show satisfactory electrochemical performances at −40, 25, and 60 °C. This further confirms the excellent Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance conferred by the unique structure of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II. These results underscore the substantial potential of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II in practical applications as SIB anode.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202404263-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/ab8d4931-b992-4f6f-99d8-2214295d9cfb/adfm202404263-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/ab8d4931-b992-4f6f-99d8-2214295d9cfb/adfm202404263-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/24b105d4-257b-40f4-bcb3-552e3e63bcf8/adfm202404263-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/ab8d4931-b992-4f6f-99d8-2214295d9cfb/adfm202404263-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202404263-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202404263" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performances of full cells at −40–60 °C. a) Charge/discharge profiles and corresponding b) Cycling curve at 0.1 C. c) Rate curve and corresponding d–f) Energy density and charge time at d) −40, e) 25, and f) 60 °C. g) Cycling stability at 1 C. h) Optical image of LED arrays powered by a single full cell. i) Schematic illustration of sodium ion storage mechanism in FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Based on the comprehensive electrochemical results, the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode material demonstrates excellent sodium storage performance over a wide temperature range. Overall, this can be attributed to the following two aspects, as illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202404263-fig-0005">5i</a>: 1) The Fe-MoS<sub>2</sub>-NOC has low Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion energy barriers, minimal temperature-dependent variation in Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion barriers, and a reduced bandgap (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S48–S51</a>, Supporting Information). These attributes guarantee the rapid transport of sodium ions in the FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II electrode during initial intercalation reactions. 2) The doped Fe atoms can be transformed into superparamagnetic Fe nanocrystals in the ensuing conversion reaction, inducing robust spin-polarized surface capacitance that enhances Na<sup>+</sup> storage. These combined factors underpin the superior electrochemical performances of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II in SIBs across a wide operation temperature range.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202404263-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202404263-sec-0070-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>To conclude, the Fe-MoS<sub>2</sub>-NOC with a monolayer Fe-doped MoS<sub>2</sub>/N,O co-doped C overlapping structure is successfully constructed and employed as anode for SIBs operating across a wide temperature range. The Fe-MoS<sub>2</sub>-NOC displays a bandgap of ∼0&nbsp;eV, an enlarged interlayer distance (11.6 Å), and low Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion barriers of 0.16&nbsp;eV (−40 °C), 0.12&nbsp;eV (25 °C), and 0.09&nbsp;eV (60 °C). In situ TEM and Ex situ XRD, XPS, and TEM reveal the intercalation and conversion reaction mechanism of sodium ion storage of FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C, in which the doped Fe atoms and MoS<sub>2</sub> can be converted into superparamagnetic Fe with the size of ∼2&nbsp;nm, Mo, and Na<sub>2</sub>S during first sodiation process, and the Fe can be oxidated into FeS<sub>2</sub> but Mo does not during desodiation process. In situ magnetometry reveals that strong spin-polarized surface capacitance can be induced by superparamagnetic Fe conversion over a wide operation temperature range, which totally dominants the sodium ion storage and transport to supply extra capacity and ensure fast ion transport stably between 0.01 and 1&nbsp;V, thus endowing FeMoS<sub>2</sub>/C-II with high capacity, excellent fast-charging performances, and long cycling life from −40 to 60 °C in half and full cells. These findings offer new insights into the use of 3d transition metal heteroatom doping strategies for conversion-type electrode materials and demonstrate the effectiveness of spin-polarized surface capacitance effect on boosting fast ion transport over a wide temperature range, especially at extremely low temperatures, which may open new avenues for designing wide-temperature-range energy storage materials.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
